        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits'. Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript.


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          The study aims to develop a novel computational approach, PhenoPLIER,
          that can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential
          targets missed by single-gene strategies. The method maps gene-trait
          associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
          latent representation, based on modules of genes with similar
          expression patterns across different conditions. The study shows that
          diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in
          relevant cell types and that PhenoPLIER is accurate in predicting
          known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action.

          lacking associations are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER through a CRISPR screen analysis of lipid regulation.
          Overall, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting
          genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, which can
          improve our understanding of disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits'. Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript, so it has a clear sentence structure and
          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.


          Revised paragraph:
        display: >-
          /home/miltondp/projects/others/manubot/manubot-ai-editor-evals/abstract/phenoplier/prompts/candidate.txt
      vars: *ref_1
      response:
        output: >-

          Gene expression patterns are critical for understanding the functions
          of genes in specific contexts. However, determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. Traditional
          approaches that focus on single-gene analyses have limitations in
          capturing gene-gene interactions and their role in disease development
          and progression. Here, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational
          approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological
          perturbation data into a common latent representation for a joint
          analysis. This approach is based on modules of genes with similar
          expression patterns across the same conditions, allowing for more
          accurate prediction of known drug-disease pairs and inference of
          mechanisms of action. Our results show that diseases are significantly
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and
          PhenoPLIER can prioritize functionally important players lacking
          associations but present in trait-associated modules. By incorporating
          groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework
          for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene
          modules, revealing potential targets missed by single-gene strategies
          and contextualizing genetic associations.

        display: >-
          /home/miltondp/projects/others/manubot/manubot-ai-editor-evals/abstract/phenoplier/prompts/baseline.txt
      vars: *ref_1
      response:
        output: >-

          Genes are part of intricate networks that work together to perform
          specific functions in a given context. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires an understanding of expression
          regulation across different conditions. While individual gene studies
          have provided valuable insights into disease-relevant mechanisms,
          modern models of the architecture of complex traits predict that
          gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease development and
          progression. In this study, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational
          approach that integrates gene expression patterns, trait associations,
          and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
          representation for joint analysis. By clustering genes with similar
          expression patterns across the same conditions, our approach reveals
          that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed
          in relevant cell types. Our approach is accurate in predicting known
          drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore,
          using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that
          functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized
          in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Overall, PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules and can contextualize these
          associations to reveal potential targets missed by single-gene
          strategies.

      vars: *ref_1
      response:
        output: >-

          In the field of genetic studies, determining how genes influence
          complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of expression
          regulation across different conditions. While transcriptome-wide
          association studies have helped uncover the role of individual genes
          in disease-relevant mechanisms, modern models of the architecture of
          complex traits predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role
          in disease origin and progression. To address this gap in knowledge,
          we present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait
          associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
          latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation is
          based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the
          same conditions, allowing us to contextualize genetic associations and
          reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. Our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. We further demonstrate the utility of
          PhenoPLIER by using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation,
          finding that functionally important players lack associations but are
          prioritized in trait-associated modules. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules, highlighting the importance of
          grouping genes with similar expression patterns and providing insights
          into disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

          Genes function together in specific contexts to perform their
          functions, and understanding the regulatory mechanisms of gene
          expression across different conditions is crucial for developing new
          therapies. Although transcriptome-wide association studies have been
          successful in identifying individual genes associated with complex
          traits, modern models predict that gene-gene interactions play a
          significant role in disease origin and progression. Here, we introduce
          PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations
          and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
          representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on
          modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
          conditions. We find that diseases are significantly associated with
          gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach
          accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of
          action. Additionally, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid

          associations but were prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. Overall, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for
          contextualizing genetic associations through the lens of gene modules
          and reveals potential targets missed by single-gene strategies.

          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          /home/miltondp/projects/others/manubot/manubot-ai-editor-evals/abstract/phenoplier/prompts/candidate.txt
      vars: *ref_1
      response:
        output: >-

          In recent years, the field of functional genomics has been rapidly
          advancing our understanding of complex traits, such as diseases and
          disorders. However, genes act in concert with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. This is critical
          for developing new therapies that target specific pathways involved in
          disease etiology and drug mechanisms.


          To fill this gap, we have developed PhenoPLIER, a computational
          approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological
          perturbation data into a common latent representation for a joint
          analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with
          similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We observe
          that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed
          in relevant cell types, and our approach is accurate in predicting
          known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action.
          Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we
          find that functionally important players lack associations but are
          prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER.


          In conclusion, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting
          genetic associations through the lens of gene modules. By
          incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can
          contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed
          by single-gene strategies. This approach has the potential to
          revolutionize our understanding of complex traits and accelerate the
          development of new therapies that target specific pathways involved in
          disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

          Gene expression patterns play a critical role in determining complex
          traits and disease mechanisms. However, modern models of complex trait
          architecture suggest that gene-gene interactions are crucial for
          disease initiation and progression. In this manuscript, we present
          PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait

          conclusion, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting

          the importance of understanding gene-gene interactions in disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms.

          understanding of expression regulation across different conditions. We
          have demonstrated the importance of this insight in developing new
          therapies, as it has been shown to be critical for identifying drug
          repurposing opportunities and predicting therapeutic targets. To
          address this challenge, we used transcriptome-wide association studies
          (TWAS) to uncover the role of individual genes in disease mechanisms.
          However, recent models of complex traits suggest that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease etiology and progression.
          Our approach, PhenoPLIER, is based on modules of genes with similar
          expression patterns across the same conditions. We find that diseases
          are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant
          cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease
          pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Additionally, we show that
          functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized
          in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER
          can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets
          missed by single-gene strategies, providing a novel framework for
          interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules.
          Our findings highlight the importance of functional genomics in
          identifying therapeutic targets and drug repurposing opportunities for
          complex traits.

          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach
          that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation
          data into a common latent representation for a joint analysis. Genes
          act in concert with each other in specific contexts to perform their
          functions. Determining how these genes influence complex traits
          requires a mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across
          different conditions. It has been shown that this insight is critical
          for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies
          have helped uncover the role of individual genes in disease-relevant
          mechanisms. However, modern models of the architecture of complex
          traits predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in
          disease origin and progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is based
          on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
          conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with
          gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is
          accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          In the field of genetic studies, identifying functional genomics and
          gene co-expression patterns is critical for understanding disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms. However, current models of complex

          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. Our approach
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules, which has broader significance in
          drug repurposing and clustering of complex traits.

          Genetic studies have long been at the forefront of disease etiology
          and drug mechanism discovery, but recent advances in functional
          genomics have revealed that genes act in concert with each other to
          perform their functions. The identification of these gene modules has
          been instrumental in understanding the underlying mechanisms of
          complex traits and developing new therapies. However, traditional
          approaches for analyzing transcriptome-wide association studies have
          limitations in identifying gene-gene interactions, which are critical
          for understanding disease origin and progression. To overcome these
          challenges, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach
          that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation
          data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. Our
          method identifies modules of genes with similar expression patterns
          across the same conditions and observes that diseases are
          significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell
          types. Furthermore, our approach accurately predicts known
          drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Using a CRISPR
          screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally
          important players lack associations but are prioritized in
          trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Our results show that by
          incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can
          contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed
          by single-gene strategies. Overall, PhenoPLIER provides a novel
          framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of
          gene modules, which will have broader significance in disease etiology
          and drug mechanism discovery.

          The field of functional genomics is rapidly evolving, and researchers
          are constantly seeking novel methods to understand the complex
          interactions between genes and disease mechanisms. One significant
          challenge in this field is to identify therapeutic targets that can be
          repurposed to treat complex diseases. This challenge arises from the
          fact that modern models predict that gene-gene interactions play a
          crucial role in disease etiology. However, traditional single-gene
          approaches cannot capture these interactions and may miss potential
          targets. To address this gap, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational

          PhenoPLIER. These findings suggest that by incorporating groups of
          co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations
          and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies.
          Overall, our work provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic
          associations through the lens of gene modules and highlights the
          importance of considering gene-gene interactions in disease etiology
          and drug mechanisms.

          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits'. Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript.


          Input paragraph: We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach
          that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation
          data into a common latent representation for a joint analysis. Genes
          act in concert with each other in specific contexts to perform their
          functions. Determining how these genes influence complex traits
          requires a mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across
          different conditions. It has been shown that this insight is critical
          for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies
          have helped uncover the role of individual genes in disease-relevant
          mechanisms. However, modern models of the architecture of complex
          traits predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in
          disease origin and progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is based
          on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
          conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with
          gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is
          accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          Our study presents PhenoPLIER, a computational method that integrates
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          unified latent representation for joint analysis. We demonstrate that
          genes collaborate with each other in specific contexts to execute
          their functions, and this collaboration is critical in the development
          of new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have revealed
          the role of individual genes in disease mechanisms; however, modern
          models of complex trait architecture predict that gene-gene
          interactions are crucial for disease genesis and progression. In this

          players that lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated
          modules by PhenoPLIER. Our findings suggest that by contextualizing
          genetic associations with groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can
          provide novel insights into potential targets missed by single-gene
          strategies. Overall, our study presents a novel framework for
          interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules.

          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").

          The field of functional genomics has made significant strides in
          understanding the complex interactions between genes and diseases.
          However, modern models of disease etiology suggest that gene-gene
          interactions play a critical role in disease origin and progression.
          To address this gap in our current understanding of disease
          mechanisms, we present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. By utilizing gene
          modules with similar expression patterns across the same conditions,
          PhenoPLIER is able to identify disease-associated genes in relevant
          cell types, accurately predict known drug-disease pairs, and infer
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, we demonstrate the utility of
          PhenoPLIER by using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation,
          revealing functionally important players that lack associations but
          are prioritized in trait-associated modules. Our findings provide
          evidence for the potential role of gene modules in disease etiology
          and suggest that PhenoPLIER can be used as a novel framework for
          interpreting genetic associations.

          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies. Our
          results in this study show that diseases are significantly associated
          with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach
          is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          Genetic studies have revolutionized our understanding of disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms. However, the complexity of gene
          expression patterns in different contexts poses a challenge for
          identifying functional genomic insights that can lead to new
          therapeutic targets. In this study, we used gene co-expression

          approaches. Our approach, PhenoPLIER, was able to accurately predict

          PhenoPLIER. Overall, our findings provide a novel framework for

          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies. Our
          results in this study show that diseases are significantly associated
          with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach
          is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          Genetic studies have shown that genes act in concert with each other
          to perform their functions. However, determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. This insight is
          critical for developing new therapies, as it allows researchers to
          identify potential drug targets and predict their effectiveness. In
          this study, we used gene co-expression analysis to project genetic
          associations onto specific tissue types and disease states. Our

          contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed

          of considering the broader context in which genes act when studying

          specific contexts to perform their functions. However, understanding
          the influence of these genes on complex traits requires a deeper
          understanding of expression regulation across different conditions.

          mechanisms. However, modern models of the architecture of complex

          In recent years, genes have been found to act in concert with each
          other in specific contexts, and determining how these genes influence
          complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of expression
          regulation across different conditions. While transcriptome-wide
          association studies have helped uncover the role of individual genes
          in disease-relevant mechanisms, modern models of the architecture of
          complex traits predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role
          in disease origin and progression. To address this gap in the
          literature, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that
          maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data
          into a common latent representation for a joint analysis. Our approach

          therapeutic target discovery tool. Additionally, we use a CRISPR
          screen to analyze lipid regulation and find that functionally
          important players lack associations but are prioritized in
          trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER, further validating our
          approach. Overall, our work bridges the gap between gene expression
          studies and functional genomics, providing a novel computational tool
          for identifying therapeutic targets and drug repurposing.

          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER.

          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").

          Gene expression patterns play a crucial role in disease etiology and
          drug mechanisms. However, traditional genetic studies and functional
          genomics approaches have limitations in understanding the complex
          interactions between genes and traits. To address this gap, we
          developed PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait
          associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
          latent representation for joint analysis. Our method identifies
          modules of genes with similar expression patterns across different
          conditions and demonstrates the importance of these modules in disease
          development and drug response. We show that diseases are significantly

          approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers
          mechanisms of action. Additionally, we use a CRISPR screen to analyze

          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. Our findings provide new insights into the complex
          interplay between genes, traits, and diseases, and have broader
          significance for drug discovery and precision medicine.

          traits and disease etiology. However, a mechanistic understanding of
          gene expression regulation across different contexts is crucial for
          developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have
          revealed the role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms,
          but modern models of the architecture of complex traits predict that
          gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and
          progression. To address this challenge, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a
          computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and
          pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation
          for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes
          with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We find
          that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed
          in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known
          drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Additionally,
          using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we identify
          functionally important players lacking associations but prioritized in
          trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Our findings highlight the
          importance of considering gene expression patterns in disease etiology
          and drug mechanism studies, and provide insights for therapeutic
          targets and drug repurposing strategies.

          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").

        output: >-

          The interplay between genes in specific contexts is critical for
          understanding complex traits and developing new therapies. While
          transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms, modern models of
          complex trait architecture predict that gene-gene interactions play a
          crucial role in disease origin and progression. To address this gap,
          we present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait
          associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
          latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based
          on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
          conditions. Our results show that diseases are significantly
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers
          mechanisms of action. Additionally, we use a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation and find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. These findings highlight the importance of considering
          gene-gene interactions in disease etiology and drug mechanisms, and
          provide insights into potential therapeutic targets and drug
          repurposing opportunities.

              Genes are part of intricate networks that work together to perform
              specific functions in a given context. Determining how these genes
              influence complex traits requires an understanding of expression
              regulation across different conditions. While individual gene
              studies have provided valuable insights into disease-relevant
              mechanisms, modern models of the architecture of complex traits
              predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease
              development and progression. In this study, we introduce
              PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene
              expression patterns, trait associations, and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint
              analysis. By clustering genes with similar expression patterns
              across the same conditions, our approach reveals that diseases are
              significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant
              cell types. Our approach is accurate in predicting known
              drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action.
              Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we
              find that functionally important players lack associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Overall,
              PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic
              associations through the lens of gene modules and can
              contextualize these associations to reveal potential targets
              missed by single-gene strategies.

              In the field of genetic studies, determining how genes influence
              complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of expression
              regulation across different conditions. While transcriptome-wide
              association studies have helped uncover the role of individual
              genes in disease-relevant mechanisms, modern models of the
              architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene interactions

              action. We further demonstrate the utility of PhenoPLIER by using
              a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, finding that
              functionally important players lack associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER
              provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
              through the lens of gene modules, highlighting the importance of
              grouping genes with similar expression patterns and providing
              insights into disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

              Genes function together in specific contexts to perform their
              functions, and understanding the regulatory mechanisms of gene
              expression across different conditions is crucial for developing
              new therapies. Although transcriptome-wide association studies
              have been successful in identifying individual genes associated
              with complex traits, modern models predict that gene-gene
              interactions play a significant role in disease origin and
              progression. Here, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational
              approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint
              analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with
              similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We find
              that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules
              expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately
              predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action.
              Additionally, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation,
              we found that functionally important players lacked associations
              but were prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER.
              Overall, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for contextualizing
              genetic associations through the lens of gene modules and reveals
              potential targets missed by single-gene strategies.

            text: >-

              In recent years, the field of functional genomics has been rapidly
              advancing our understanding of complex traits, such as diseases
              and disorders. However, genes act in concert with each other in
              specific contexts to perform their functions. Determining how
              these genes influence complex traits requires a mechanistic
              understanding of expression regulation across different
              conditions. This is critical for developing new therapies that
              target specific pathways involved in disease etiology and drug
              mechanisms.


              To fill this gap, we have developed PhenoPLIER, a computational
              approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a common latent representation for a joint
              analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with
              similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We observe
              that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules
              expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is accurate in
              predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of
              action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
              regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
              associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
              PhenoPLIER.


              In conclusion, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for
              interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene
              modules. By incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER
              can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential
              targets missed by single-gene strategies. This approach has the
              potential to revolutionize our understanding of complex traits and
              accelerate the development of new therapies that target specific
              pathways involved in disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

            text: >-

              Gene expression patterns play a critical role in determining
              complex traits and disease mechanisms. However, modern models of
              complex trait architecture suggest that gene-gene interactions are
              crucial for disease initiation and progression. In this
              manuscript, we present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that
              integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint
              analysis. By mapping genes with similar expression patterns across
              different conditions, our approach can identify modules of
              functionally important players that are associated with
              disease-relevant traits and drug mechanisms. We demonstrate that
              PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers
              mechanisms of action using a CRISPR screen for lipid regulation.
              Our findings suggest that by incorporating groups of co-expressed
              genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and
              reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. In
              conclusion, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting
              genetic associations through the lens of gene modules,
              highlighting the importance of understanding gene-gene
              interactions in disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

              Genes work together in specific contexts to perform their
              functions. Understanding how genes influence complex traits
              requires a comprehensive understanding of expression regulation
              across different conditions. This knowledge is critical for
              developing new therapies. While transcriptome-wide association
              studies have helped identify the role of individual genes in
              disease-relevant mechanisms, modern models of complex trait
              architecture predict that gene-gene interactions are crucial in
              disease origin and progression. In this study, we present

              mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to

              provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
              through the lens of gene modules, which can contextualize genetic

              strategies.

            text: >-

              The field of functional genomics has shed light on the importance
              of gene expression patterns in complex traits, but there is still
              a gap in our understanding of how individual genes interact to
              influence these traits. This gap matters because it limits our
              ability to develop effective therapies for diseases that involve
              multiple genes. In this study, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a
              computational approach that leverages gene expression patterns
              across different conditions and drug perturbations to map
              gene-trait associations into a common latent representation. Using
              this representation, we demonstrate that diseases are
              significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant
              cell types and accurately predict known drug-disease pairs and
              infer mechanisms of action. Additionally, using a CRISPR screen,
              we identify functionally important players that lack individual
              gene associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules.
              In conclusion, by considering groups of co-expressed genes,
              PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic
              associations and reveals potential targets missed by single-gene
              strategies, opening up new avenues for drug repurposing and
              therapeutic target discovery.

              In this study, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach
              for mapping gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a common latent representation. Our
              analysis shows that genes work together in specific contexts to
              perform their functions. Determining how these genes influence
              complex traits requires an understanding of expression regulation
              across different conditions. We have demonstrated the importance
              of this insight in developing new therapies, as it has been shown
              to be critical for identifying drug repurposing opportunities and
              predicting therapeutic targets. To address this challenge, we used
              transcriptome-wide association studies (TWAS) to uncover the role
              of individual genes in disease mechanisms. However, recent models
              of complex traits suggest that gene-gene interactions play a
              crucial role in disease etiology and progression. Our approach,
              PhenoPLIER, is based on modules of genes with similar expression
              patterns across the same conditions. We find that diseases are
              significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant
              cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known
              drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Additionally,
              we show that functionally important players lack associations but
              are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In
              conclusion, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and
              reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies,
              providing a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
              through the lens of gene modules. Our findings highlight the
              importance of functional genomics in identifying therapeutic
              targets and drug repurposing opportunities for complex traits.

              perform their functions. Determining how these genes influence
              complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of expression
              regulation across different conditions. It has been shown that
              this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
              Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the
              role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However,
              modern models of the architecture of complex traits predict that
              gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and
              progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is based on modules of
              genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions.
              We observe that diseases are significantly associated with gene
              modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is
              accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
              mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to
              analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important
              players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated
              modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of
              co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic
              associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene
              strategies. PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting
              genetic associations through the lens of gene modules.

              In the field of genetic studies, identifying functional genomics

              In this study, we present PhenoPLIER, a computational tool that
              integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data to produce a joint analysis. Gene expression
              patterns are critical for understanding complex traits as they act
              in concert with one another in specific contexts. We have
              demonstrated the importance of this insight in developing new
              therapies, and transcriptome-wide association studies have helped
              uncover individual genes' roles in disease-relevant mechanisms.
              However, recent models predict that gene-gene interactions play a
              crucial role in disease etiology and progression. PhenoPLIER's
              representation is based on modules of genes with similar
              expression patterns across the same conditions. Our analysis shows
              that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules
              expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately
              predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action.
              Furthermore, we use a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation
              and find that functionally important players lack associations but
              are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In
              conclusion, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting
              genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, which is
              critical for contextualizing complex traits and identifying
              potential drug targets missed by single-gene strategies. Our
              approach combines functional genomics with therapeutic target
              discovery and drug repurposing, ultimately leading to clustering
              of complex traits and providing insights into disease etiology and
              mechanisms.

              Genetic studies have long been at the forefront of disease
              etiology and drug mechanism discovery, but recent advances in
              functional genomics have revealed that genes act in concert with
              each other to perform their functions. The identification of these
              gene modules has been instrumental in understanding the underlying
              mechanisms of complex traits and developing new therapies.
              However, traditional approaches for analyzing transcriptome-wide
              association studies have limitations in identifying gene-gene
              interactions, which are critical for understanding disease origin
              and progression. To overcome these challenges, we introduce
              PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach that maps gene-trait
              associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
              latent representation for joint analysis. Our method identifies
              modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
              conditions and observes that diseases are significantly associated
              with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types. Furthermore,
              our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and
              infers mechanisms of action. Using a CRISPR screen to analyze
              lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
              associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
              PhenoPLIER. Our results show that by incorporating groups of
              co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic
              associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene
              strategies. Overall, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for
              interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene
              modules, which will have broader significance in disease etiology
              and drug mechanism discovery.

              In this study, we present PhenoPLIER, a computational tool that
              integrates gene expression data and pharmacological perturbation
              information to create a common latent representation for joint
              analysis. The approach recognizes the importance of gene networks
              in regulating complex traits and disease development. We
              demonstrate the utility of PhenoPLIER by analyzing
              transcriptome-wide association studies, revealing that diseases
              are associated with specific groups of genes expressed in relevant
              cell types. Furthermore, our method accurately predicts known
              drug-disease pairs and suggests new mechanisms of action.
              Moreover, we use a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation and
              find that functionally important players lack associations but are
              prioritized within trait-associated gene modules. Overall,
              PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic
              associations in the context of gene networks, enabling the
              identification of potential therapeutic targets and drug
              repurposing opportunities.

            text: >-

              The field of functional genomics is rapidly evolving, and
              researchers are constantly seeking novel methods to understand the
              complex interactions between genes and disease mechanisms. One
              significant challenge in this field is to identify therapeutic
              targets that can be repurposed to treat complex diseases. This
              challenge arises from the fact that modern models predict that
              gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease etiology.
              However, traditional single-gene approaches cannot capture these
              interactions and may miss potential targets. To address this gap,
              we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates
              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into
              a common latent representation for joint analysis. Our method uses
              modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
              conditions to identify disease-relevant gene modules expressed in
              relevant cell types. We show that our approach accurately predicts
              known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action, and we
              also find that functionally important players lack associations
              but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER.
              These findings suggest that by incorporating groups of
              co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic
              associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene
              strategies. Overall, our work provides a novel framework for
              interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules
              and highlights the importance of considering gene-gene
              interactions in disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

              progression. To address this gap in our current understanding of
              disease mechanisms, we present PhenoPLIER, a computational
              approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a common latent representation for a joint
              analysis. By utilizing gene modules with similar expression
              patterns across the same conditions, PhenoPLIER is able to
              identify disease-associated genes in relevant cell types,
              accurately predict known drug-disease pairs, and infer mechanisms
              of action. Furthermore, we demonstrate the utility of PhenoPLIER
              by using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, revealing
              functionally important players that lack associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules. Our findings provide
              evidence for the potential role of gene modules in disease
              etiology and suggest that PhenoPLIER can be used as a novel
              framework for interpreting genetic associations.

              integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological

              The current state of the art in genetic studies has primarily
              focused on identifying individual genes associated with
              disease-relevant mechanisms, but it is widely recognized that
              gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and
              progression. To address this gap, we present PhenoPLIER, a
              computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and
              pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
              representation for joint analysis. Our method identifies modules
              of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
              conditions, which enables us to contextualize genetic associations
              and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies.


              Using PhenoPLIER, we observe that diseases are significantly
              associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and
              our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and
              infers mechanisms of action. Furthermore, we found that
              functionally important players lack associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. These
              results highlight the potential of PhenoPLIER to facilitate
              disease etiology studies and drug mechanism discovery by providing
              a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through
              the lens of gene modules. Overall, PhenoPLIER offers a promising
              tool for identifying therapeutic targets missed by single-gene
              strategies, which could lead to more effective treatments for
              complex diseases.

              ---


              Genetic studies have shown that genes interact with each other in
              specific contexts to perform their functions. However,
              understanding the influence of these genes on complex traits
              requires a deeper understanding of expression regulation across
              different conditions. This insight is critical for developing new
              therapies, and transcriptome-wide association studies have been
              instrumental in uncovering the role of individual genes in
              disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern models of the
              architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene interactions
              play a crucial role in disease origin and progression. In this
              study, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into
              a common latent representation for a joint analysis. This
              representation is based on modules of genes with similar
              expression patterns across the same conditions. We found that
              diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed
              in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known
              drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Furthermore,
              using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we found that
              functionally important players lack associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. These
              findings highlight the importance of gene co-expression in disease
              etiology and drug mechanism.

            text: >-

              In recent years, genes have been found to act in concert with each
              other in specific contexts, and determining how these genes
              influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
              expression regulation across different conditions. While
              transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the
              role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms, modern
              models of the architecture of complex traits predict that
              gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and
              progression. To address this gap in the literature, we introduce
              PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait
              associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
              latent representation for a joint analysis. Our approach is based
              on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the
              same conditions and observes that diseases are significantly
              associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types. We
              demonstrate that PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease
              pairs and infers mechanisms of action, highlighting its potential
              as a therapeutic target discovery tool. Additionally, we use a
              CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation and find that
              functionally important players lack associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER, further
              validating our approach. Overall, our work bridges the gap between
              gene expression studies and functional genomics, providing a novel
              computational tool for identifying therapeutic targets and drug
              repurposing.

              Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
              contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
              influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
              expression regulation across different conditions. It has been
              shown that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
              Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the
              role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However,
              modern models of the architecture of complex traits predict that
              gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and
              progression. Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational
              approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological

              similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We observe
              that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules

              predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of
              action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
              regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
              associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
              PhenoPLIER.
