              The current study highlights the importance of functional genomics
              and gene co-expression analysis in understanding complex traits,
              disease mechanisms, and therapeutic targets. We propose a novel
              computational approach called PhenoPLIER, which integrates gene
              expression data with pharmacological perturbation information to
              identify modules of genes associated with specific traits. Our
              analysis reveals that diseases are often associated with modules
              expressed in relevant cell types and accurately predicts known
              drug-disease pairs. Furthermore, we demonstrate the effectiveness
              of our approach by using a CRISPR screen to identify important
              players in lipid regulation that lack direct associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules. Our findings suggest that
              PhenoPLIER could be a valuable tool for drug repurposing and
              identifying new therapeutic targets for complex diseases.

            text: >-

              Gene expression patterns play a crucial role in disease etiology
              and drug mechanisms. However, traditional genetic studies and
              functional genomics approaches have limitations in understanding
              the complex interactions between genes and traits. To address this
              gap, we developed PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into
              a common latent representation for joint analysis. Our method
              identifies modules of genes with similar expression patterns
              across different conditions and demonstrates the importance of
              these modules in disease development and drug response. We show
              that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules
              expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately
              predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action.
              Additionally, we use a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation
              and identify functionally important players that lack associations
              but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Our
              findings provide new insights into the complex interplay between
              genes, traits, and diseases, and have broader significance for
              drug discovery and precision medicine.

            text: >-

              The genetic architecture of complex traits involves the
              interaction of multiple genes in specific contexts. Understanding
              gene expression regulation across different conditions is crucial
              for developing new therapies and understanding disease mechanisms.
              Transcriptome-wide association studies have identified individual
              genes involved in disease-relevant processes, but modern models
              suggest that gene-gene interactions are essential to disease
              origin and progression. In this study, we present PhenoPLIER, a
              computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and
              pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
              representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on
              modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
              conditions. We find that diseases are significantly associated
              with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
              approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers
              mechanisms of action. Additionally, we use a CRISPR screen to
              analyze lipid regulation and demonstrate that functionally
              important players lacking associations are prioritized in
              trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Our study highlights the
              importance of considering gene expression patterns and
              interactions in understanding complex traits, disease etiology,
              and drug mechanisms.

            namedScores: *ref_49
            text: >-

              Gene expression patterns are a critical aspect of disease etiology
              and drug mechanisms. To better understand how genes interact in
              specific contexts, it is essential to have a mechanistic
              understanding of expression regulation across different
              conditions. Genetic studies and functional genomics have been
              instrumental in uncovering the role of individual genes in
              disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern models of complex
              traits predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in
              disease origin and progression. To address this challenge, we
              developed PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into
              a common latent representation for joint analysis. This
              representation is based on modules of genes with similar
              expression patterns across the same conditions. We found that
              diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed
              in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known
              drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Additionally,
              using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we discovered
              that functionally important players lack associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Overall,
              our findings highlight the importance of gene expression patterns
              in disease etiology and drug mechanisms, and demonstrate the
              utility of computational approaches in identifying therapeutic
              targets and repurposing drugs.

              Gene expression patterns play a crucial role in disease etiology
              and drug mechanisms. However, determining how genes interact with
              each other to perform their functions is challenging. This
              requires a mechanistic understanding of expression regulation
              across different conditions. Traditional approaches to studying
              gene-gene interactions are limited by the lack of comprehensive
              data on gene expression patterns. To address this challenge, we

              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into
              a common latent representation for a joint analysis. Our approach

              and inferring mechanisms of action using CRISPR screens. Our
              findings highlight the importance of understanding gene expression

            text: >-

              The interplay between genes in specific contexts is critical for
              understanding complex traits and developing new therapies. While
              transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the
              role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms, modern
              models of complex trait architecture predict that gene-gene
              interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and
              progression. To address this gap, we present PhenoPLIER, a
              computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and
              pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
              representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on
              modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
              conditions. Our results show that diseases are significantly
              associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and
              our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and
              infers mechanisms of action. Additionally, we use a CRISPR screen
              to analyze lipid regulation and find that functionally important
              players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated
              modules by PhenoPLIER. These findings highlight the importance of
              considering gene-gene interactions in disease etiology and drug
              mechanisms, and provide insights into potential therapeutic
              targets and drug repurposing opportunities.
            prompt: >-
              You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
              improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
              associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
              etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
              functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
              repurposing, clustering of complex traits'. Revise the following
              abstract of this manuscript, so it has a clear sentence structure
              and follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits
              in a single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely
              necessary to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the
              abstract must follow the following structure: 1) The context must
              communicate to the reader what gap the paper will fill. The first
              sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
              which the particular research is situated. Then, this context is
              narrowed until it lands on the open question that the research
              answered. A successful context section sets the stage for
              distinguishing the paper’s contributions from the current state of
              the art by communicating what is missing in the literature (i.e.,
              the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e., the connection
              between the specific gap and the broader context that the paper
              opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the novel
              method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question. Then
              you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
              Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the
              question that was posed at the end of the context section. There
              is often a second part to the conclusion section that highlights
              how this conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e.,
              "broader significance").
